Bacillus anthracis	38	Bacillus anthracis str. Ames	NC_003997	AE016879			FGS/MOD/UPR	This is the first genome of Bacillus anthracis. Bacillus anthracis is a pathogenic bacterium causing lethal inhalational anthrax. Key virulence genes are found on plasmids pXO1 and pXO2. The B. anthracis Ames Ancestor strain originally isolated from a dead cow in Texas in 1981 and is used as a &apos;gold standard&apos; for development of vaccines and testing their effectiveness in the United States. The reference laboratory sample (Porton isolate) has been derived from Ancestor and cured of plasmid pXO1 and pXO2. The Ames strain (Florida) became subject to intensive study after its use in 2001 anthrax letter attacks in Florida. B.anthracis is a highly monomorphic species with genes from different isolates having more than 99% nucleotide sequence identity. However different isolates show high phenotypic variation in infection potential.	12721629	http://www.uniprot.org/taxonomy/?query=reference:yes%20ancestor:3

Escherichia coli	1780	Escherichia coli O157:H7 str. Sakai	NC_002695	BA000007	NC_002127 ... (2)	AB011548 ... (2)	PHY/CLI	This pathogenic strain of E. coli is enterohemorrhagic and a cause of foodborne illness. Most cases of food poisoning have been linked with eating undercooked contaminated ground meat, raw contaminated vegetables or unpasteurized milk. Waterborne transmission occurs by swimming in contaminated lakes or pools, or by drinking contaminated water. The organism is communicable person-to-person and has caused outbreaks in child day-care centers. E. coli O157:H7 requires specific receptors in order to attach to and enter intestinal cells. Cattle, swine, and deer do not have these receptors, and so can harbor the strain in their intestines without ill effect. The strain contaminated meat during slaughter or butchering, and when undercooked meat is eaten causes acute hemorrhagic diarrhea and abdominal cramps. In healthy adults, the symptoms subside in 5-10 days. In children and the elderly, the infection can cause hemolytic uremic syndrome (2-7% of cases), in which the red blood cells are destroyed and the kidneys fail. This strain is the representative of E. coli sub-clade E.	10734605,11108008,11111050,11258796	http://www.genome.wisc.edu/; http://ecocyc.org/

Escherichia coli	1780	Escherichia coli str. K-12 substr. MG1655	NC_000913	U00096			PHY/FGS/MOD/UPR	E. coli K-12 was one of the first organisms to have its genome sequenced, and as such has become a model organism in microbiology research. It is well-adapted to the laboratory environment, and has lost the ability to survive in the intestine. This non-pathogenic laboratory strain was orginally isolated from a stool sample of a patient with diptheria in 1922. During the course of lab culturing, it lost the O-antigen, lambda phage, and F-plasmid. Substrain MG1655 is a parent of DH5a and DH10, which are used extensively in biotechnology. This strain is the representative of E. coli sub-clade A.
